<p>Scanline VFX completed the reveal shots of the Helicarrier, from the moment Black Widow and Captain America arrive on the carrier deck to the point where it lifts off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-3"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Evil Eye Pictures composited digital backgrounds into shots filmed against a greenscreen for scenes taking place inside the Helicarrier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-4"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Colin Strause of Hydraulx said, "We did the opening ten minutes of the movie, other than the opening set-up in space" including Loki's arrival on Earth and subsequent escape from the S.H.I.E.L.D. base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-5"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Luma Pictures worked on shots featuring the Helicarrier's bridge and incorporated the graphic monitor displays that were developed by Cantina Creative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-6"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Fuel VFX completed shots taking place in and around Tony Stark's penthouse at <a href="/wiki/Stark_Tower" title="Stark Tower">Stark Tower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-7"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Digital Domain created the asteroid environment, where Loki encounters The Other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fxguide_112-8"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Method Design in Los Angeles created the film's closing credits. Steve Viola, creative director at Method Design, said, "This piece was a two-minute, self-contained main on end sequence created entirely in CG. For each of the shots in the sequence, we designed, modeled, textured, and lit all of the environments and many of the foreground objects. We received assets from Marvel to include in the piece, then heavily re-modeled and re-surfaced them to create a post-battle macro sequence. We also designed a custom typeface for the Main Title of <i>The Avengers</i> as well as 30 credits set in-scene."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWN_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(soundtrack)" title="The Avengers (soundtrack)">The Avengers (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>In November 2011, Marvel announced that <a href="/wiki/Alan_Silvestri" title="Alan Silvestri">Alan Silvestri</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">scored</a> <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i>, would write and compose the score for <i>The Avengers</i>. Silvestri said, "I've worked on films where there have been a number of stars and certainly worked on films where there have been characters of equal weight in terms of their level of importance and profile in the film, but this one is somewhat extreme in that regard because each of these characters has their own world and it's a very different situation. It's very challenging to look for a way to give everyone the weight and consideration they need, but at the same time the film is really about the coming together of these characters, which implies that there is this entity called the Avengers which really has to be representative of all of them together."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silvestri_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Silvestri-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Silvestri developed the score with the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> in London, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SXSW1_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-SXSW1-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Whedon said, "The score is very old-fashioned, which is why [Silvestri] was letter-perfect for this movie because he can give you the heightened emotion, the [<a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>] school of 'I'm just feeling a lot right now!' but he can also be extraordinarily cue and character specific, which I love."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SXSW1_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-SXSW1-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2012, American <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Soundgarden" title="Soundgarden">Soundgarden</a> announced through its Facebook page that its song "<a href="/wiki/Live_to_Rise" title="Live to Rise">Live to Rise</a>" would be included on the film's soundtrack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soundgarden_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soundgarden-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the Indian rock band <a href="/wiki/Agnee" title="Agnee">Agnee</a> released a music video for its single "Hello Andheron", which serves as the theme song for the film's Indian release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agnee_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Agnee-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The following day, Marvel revealed details for the soundtrack, which was released May 1, 2012, the same day as the score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soundtrack_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soundtrack-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/220px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/330px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/440px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fans at the film's world premiere, outside Hollywood's <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2012, Disney announced that the film's title would be changed in the United Kingdom to avoid confusion with the <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(TV_series)" title="The Avengers (TV series)">British TV series of the same name</a>, as well as its <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(1998_film)" title="The Avengers (1998 film)">1998 film adaptation</a>. This led to confusion over the film's actual title. <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine reported that the film would be titled <i>Marvel Avengers Assemble</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AvengersAssemble2_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAssemble2-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> said that it would be called simply <i>Avengers Assemble</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AvengersAssemble_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAssemble-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Marvel's UK website refers to the film as <i>Marvel's Avengers Assemble</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarvelUK_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarvelUK-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> although David Cox of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, in arguing that it was one of the worst film titles ever, considered this to be an error in the production notes, albeit grammatically clearer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cox_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification" title="British Board of Film Classification">British Board of Film Classification</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Film_Classification_Office" title="Irish Film Classification Office">Irish Film Classification Office</a>, the title is <i>Marvel Avengers Assemble</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBFC_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBFC-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFCO_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-IFCO-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lovece" title="Frank Lovece">Frank Lovece</a> in FilmFestivalTraveler.com addressed the discrepancy, writing, "<i>The Avengers</i> — formally titled <i>Marvel's The Avengers</i> onscreen, though no apostrophe-s appears on the posters..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmfestivaltraveler_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestivaltraveler-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer Kevin Feige said there are only two words in the UK title, one more than in the U.S. title, and stated that "decisions like that aren't made lightly and there are lots of marketing research, lawyers and things that get into the mix on it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspy_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film's world premiere was April 11, 2012, at Hollywood's <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premiere_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Avengers</i> closed the 11th Annual <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a> with a screening on April 28, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribeca_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribeca-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The film received an expanded one-week theatrical push for the 2012 U.S. <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> weekend, increasing the number of theaters from 123 to 1,700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaborDayPush_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaborDayPush-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film was promoted at the 2010 San Diego Comic-Con International, during which a teaser trailer narrated by Samuel L. Jackson was shown followed by an introduction of the cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregg_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2011, Marvel Studios announced that it would not hold a panel at the 2011 San Diego Comic-Con International after studio executives decided it was not prepared to compete with its own past and fan expectations with filming still in production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 2011, a teaser trailer that was meant to be the post-credits scene of <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i> was briefly leaked online. <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> speculated it came from a preview screening and described the footage as "shaky, fuzzy, flickering and obviously filmed on a cell phone".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW3_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW3-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20111015_NYCC-6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1060" data-file-width="1600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/220px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/330px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/440px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20111015_NYCC-6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chris Evans, Tom Hiddleston, Cobie Smulders, and Clark Gregg promoting the film at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con" title="New York Comic Con">New York Comic Con</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 2011, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pixar_Animation_Studios" title="Pixar Animation Studios">Pixar Animation Studios</a> and Marvel Studios presented a look at <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>' upcoming film slate, which included <i>The Avengers</i>, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D23_Expo" title="D23 Expo">D23 Expo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>. The presentation featured footage from the film and appearances by the cast members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D23_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-D23-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in August, Disney dismissed Marvel's executive vice president of worldwide marketing, vice president of worldwide marketing and manager of worldwide marketing to bring their functions in-house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, Marvel Studios held a presentation at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con" title="New York Comic Con">New York Comic Con</a> that featured new footage and a panel discussion including producer Kevin Feige and several cast members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCC_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCC-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The first full-length trailer was also released in October. <i><a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Resources" title="Comic Book Resources">Comic Book Resources</a></i> said, "The two-minute teaser handily establishes the movie's premise" and is "heavy on the assembling, but fans are also treated to plenty of action, as well glimpses  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] of Iron Man's new armor and, best of all, the new take on the Incredible Hulk. Naturally, Robert Downey Jr.'s Tony Stark gets the best lines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBR_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBR-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> However, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> called it, "Awesome. Or it would be if we hadn't seen all of this before and expected every single thing that we saw in the trailer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter6_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter6-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The trailer, which debuted exclusively on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes Movie Trailers</a>, was downloaded over 10 million times in its first 24 hours, breaking the website's record for the most-viewed trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessWire_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessWire-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> This record was surpassed by the trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>, which was downloaded more than 12.5 million times in its first 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketWatch_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketWatch-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> The trailer received 20.4 million views in the 24 hours after it debuted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrailerViews_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-TrailerViews-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> A second full-length trailer was released on iTunes in February 2012, reaching a record 13.7 million downloads in 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYDailyNews_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYDailyNews-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The theatrical trailers of <i>The Avengers</i> appeared with many films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_%E2%80%93_Ghost_Protocol" title="Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol">Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/21_Jump_Street_(film)" title="21 Jump Street (film)">21 Jump Street</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games_(film)" title="The Hunger Games (film)">The Hunger Games</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline5_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline5-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, Marvel Studios held a global Twitter chat. The 30-minute live tweeting event featured writer/director Joss Whedon, cast members Samuel L. Jackson, Tom Hiddleston and Clark Gregg and a 10-second tease of the 30-second <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> commercial that would air during <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a> in February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marvel2_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel2-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, Disney paid an estimated $4 million for the 30-second spot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fritz_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fritz-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 1, 2012, executives from Marvel Studios, along with actors Tom Hiddleston and Clark Gregg, rang the opening bell of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in honor of the film's theatrical release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSE_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSE-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tie-in_comics">Tie-in comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tie-in comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics">Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics</a></div>
<p>In December 2011, Marvel announced that an eight-issue comic-book prelude to the film, written by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Yost" title="Christopher Yost">Christopher Yost</a> and Eric Pearson with art by <a href="/wiki/Luke_Ross" title="Luke Ross">Luke Ross</a> and Daniel HDR, would be released in March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marvel1_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel1-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2012, Marvel announced the release of a second limited series comic book tie-in, <i>Black Widow Strikes</i> written by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Van_Lente" title="Fred Van Lente">Fred Van Lente</a>, who wrote <i>Captain America: First Vengeance</i>, the comic-book prequel to <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i>. The story is set between <i>Iron Man 2</i> and <i>The Avengers</i> and follows Black Widow as she runs down some loose ends from <i>Iron Man 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marvel3_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel3-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the title <i>Avengers Assemble</i> was launched in March 2012, written by Brian Michael Bendis with art by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bagley" title="Mark Bagley">Mark Bagley</a> and features the same Avengers line-up as the film battling a new incarnation of the supervillain team <a href="/wiki/Zodiac_(comics)" title="Zodiac (comics)">Zodiac</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schedeen_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schedeen-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_partners">Promotional partners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Promotional partners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Paul Gitter, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel Entertainment</a>'s president of consumer products, commented that the build-up to the film helped strengthen retail partnerships: "Retailers have been less tolerant with [intellectual property] films, so we decided that if we started on this coordinated strategy several years ago, retailers would give us shelf space throughout the years and we would have a more sustainable position in the marketplace".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisanti_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lisanti-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2011, set photos of Robert Downey Jr. driving a new model <a href="/wiki/Acura" title="Acura">Acura</a> were published online. An Acura spokesperson later released a statement confirming the company's involvement with the film, "As you may know, Acura has been in the Marvel Comics Universe films as the official car of their fictional law enforcement agency called S.H.I.E.L.D. That relationship continues for <i>The Avengers</i>. The open-top sports car that was photographed yesterday is a one-off, fictional car that was made just for the movie and will not be produced. That said, as you may also know, our CEO has said publicly that we are studying the development of a new sportscar, but we can't say any more about it at this time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nunez_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nunez-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2011, Acura announced that a new <a href="/wiki/Honda_NSX" title="Honda NSX">NSX</a> styled along the lines of the <a href="/wiki/Concept_car" title="Concept car">concept</a> built for <i>The Avengers</i> would be unveiled at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/North_American_International_Auto_Show" title="North American International Auto Show">North American International Auto Show</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vijayenthiran_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vijayenthiran-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> A series of 10 S.H.I.E.L.D. <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUVs</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Acura_MDX" title="Acura MDX">Acura MDX</a> with modifications by Cinema Vehicle Services, were also made for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDX_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-MDX-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012, it was announced that Marvel has partnered with fragrance company JADS to promote <i>The Avengers</i> with character-based fragrances. The announcement was just ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Toy_Industry_Association" title="Toy Industry Association">Toy Industry Association</a>'s annual February exhibition, where representatives held a sampling booth of the products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JADS_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-JADS-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Other promotional partners include bracelet-maker Colantotte, <a href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper" title="Dr Pepper">Dr Pepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farmers_Insurance_Group" title="Farmers Insurance Group">Farmers Insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson" title="Harley-Davidson">Harley-Davidson</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hershey_Company" title="The Hershey Company">Hershey</a>, Land O'Frost <a href="/wiki/Cold_cut" title="Cold cut">lunchmeats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwan_Food_Company#Red_Baron_Squadron" title="Schwan Food Company">Red Baron pizza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symantec" title="Symantec">Symantec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Wyndham Hotels &amp; Resorts">Wyndham Hotels &amp; Resorts</a>. In total, Marvel and its parent-company Disney secured an estimated $100 million in worldwide marketing support for the film. Notable exclusions include <a href="/wiki/Baskin-Robbins" title="Baskin-Robbins">Baskin-Robbins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a>, who had partnered with Marvel in the past when their films were distributed by Paramount. Disney does not generally promote through <a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a> outlets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety5_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Variety5-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game">Video game</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Video game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A video game based on the film was planned for concurrent release. The game was to be a <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a>/<a href="/wiki/Beat_%27em_up" title="Beat 'em up">brawler</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and published by <a href="/wiki/THQ" title="THQ">THQ</a>, with <a href="/wiki/THQ_Studio_Australia" title="THQ Studio Australia">THQ Studio Australia</a> developing the console versions and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Tongue_Entertainment" title="Blue Tongue Entertainment">Blue Tongue Entertainment</a> the <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">PC</a> version. After THQ closed both studios, the game was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lien_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lien-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Intellectual property rights for an Avengers video game reverted to Marvel, which said it was exploring potential publishing and licensing opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinclair_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sinclair-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a> and Marvel Entertainment announced that they were partnering to develop a motion-controlled game titled <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Avengers:_Battle_for_Earth" title="Marvel Avengers: Battle for Earth">Marvel Avengers: Battle for Earth</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> and Xbox 360 <a href="/wiki/Kinect" title="Kinect">Kinect</a>. The game was inspired by the "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Invasion" title="Secret Invasion">Secret Invasion</a>" storyline and features 20 different characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BfE_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-BfE-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> Marvel also announced a four-chapter <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> titled <i>Avengers Initiative</i>, with one chapter focusing on each of Hulk, Captain America, Thor and Iron Man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MobileGame_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-MobileGame-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film was released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HM_Magazine1_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-HM_Magazine1-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray6_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray6-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> on Blu-ray, Blu-ray 3D, DVD and <a href="/wiki/Digital_copy" title="Digital copy">digital download</a> on September 25, 2012 in the United States and as early as August 29, 2012 in various international markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray5_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray5-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer Kevin Feige said the Blu-ray features a new <a href="/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots" title="Marvel One-Shots">Marvel One-Shot</a> titled <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Item_47" title="Item 47">Item 47</a></i> and "a number of deleted scenes and a few storylines that fell by the wayside during the editing process" including "a few more scenes with the S.H.I.E.L.D. agent Maria Hill, played by Cobie Smulders" and "some slightly different versions of Maria Hill and Nick Fury's interaction with the World Security Council".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray3_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray3-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film was also released in a ten-disc box set titled <i>Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One – Avengers Assembled</i> that includes all of the "Phase One" films in the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray2_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray2-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in September 2012, the set's release, which was scheduled on the same day as the Blu-ray, was delayed until April 2, 2013, due to a pending lawsuit over the suitcase used to package the collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray4_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray4-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxset_release_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boxset_release-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Some fans have criticized the UK DVD and Blu-ray release for omitting Joss Whedon's audio commentary, and for altering the scene involving Phil Coulson's death from the film's theatrical version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKBluray_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKBluray-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> Disney's UK division said the "less graphic depiction of Agent Coulson's confrontation with Loki" occurred because "[e]ach country has its own compliance issues relative to depictions of violence. Unfortunately, another region's elements were inadvertently used to create the UK in-home release".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKBluray_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKBluray-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Upon its first week of release on home media in the U.S., the film topped the Nielsen VideoScan First Alert chart, which tracks overall disc sales, as well as the dedicated Blu-ray Disc sales chart with 72% of unit sales coming from Blu-ray, a record for a new release in which both the DVD and Blu-ray formats were released simultaneously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bluray6_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray6-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Avengers</i> grossed $623.4 million in North America and $895.2 million in other countries, for a worldwide total of $1.518 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">third highest-grossing film worldwide</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-third_highest_news_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-third_highest_news-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/2012_in_film" title="2012 in film">highest-grossing 2012 film</a>. It is the highest-grossing <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic-book</a> adaptation, the highest grossing <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> and the highest-grossing film ever released by the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-highest-Disney_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-highest-Disney-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's worldwide opening of $392.5 million is the third largest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-world-open_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-world-open-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Avengers</i> also became the fifth film distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Disney</a> and the twelfth film overall to earn more than $1 billion. It reached this milestone in 19 days, matching the record for speed previously set by <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> and <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-1billion_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-1billion-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter16_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter16-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time-1billion_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time-1billion-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> Its grosses exceeded its estimated $220 million production cost 12 days after its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoxOffice2_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoxOffice2-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> It was the first Marvel production to generate $1 billion in ticket sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TicketSales_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-TicketSales-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The film became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Not_adjusted_for_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">third highest-grossing film</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-third_highest_news_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-third_highest_news-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-domestic_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-domestic-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing 2012 film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012films_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012films-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest grossing film distributed by Disney,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-Disney_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-Disney-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing superhero film and the highest-grossing film based on comics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> It opened Friday, May 4, 2012, on around 11,800 screens across 4,349 theaters, and earned $80.8 million, marking the second-biggest opening and second-biggest single-day gross, behind <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opngday_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-opngday-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snglday_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-snglday-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's Friday gross included an $18.7 million midnight run, a record for a superhero film<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-midnight_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-midnight-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> (overtaken by <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-midnight-TDKR_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-midnight-TDKR-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Without midnight grosses, the film earned the largest opening-day gross ($62.1 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-opngday_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opngday-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> It also set a Saturday- and Sunday-gross record ($69.6 million and $57.1 million respectively).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saturday_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-saturday-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sunday_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-sunday-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, it earned a total of $207,438,708 for its debut weekend, setting an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_biggest_opening_weekends#Biggest_opening_weekends_in_U.S._and_Canada" title="List of biggest opening weekends">opening-weekend record</a>, including an IMAX opening-weekend record of $15.3 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter14_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter14-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW-opening_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-opening-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> (overtaken by <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAX-TDKR_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMAX-TDKR-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> and a record for opening-weekend grosses originating from 3D showings ($108 million), which was previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The opening-weekend audience was evenly split among those under and over the age of 25, with 60% of the audience male, 55% couples, 24% families and 21% teenagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAAudience_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAAudience-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Earning $103.1 million on its second weekend, the film set a record for the largest second-weekend gross, a record previously held by <i>Avatar</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-second_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-second-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> Other records set by the film include the biggest weekend per-theater average for a wide release ($47,698 per theater),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-average_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-average-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> the fastest film to reach $100 million and each additional $50 million through $550 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-second_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-second-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-records_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-records-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-fifth_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-fifth-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> and the largest cumulative gross through every day of release until, and including, its forty-third day (with the exception of its first day).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_weekend_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-second_weekend-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> It was in first place at the North American box office for three consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-third_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-third-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> The film set a record for the highest monthly share (previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film)" title="Spider-Man (2002 film)">Spider-Man</a></i>), with its $532.5 million total (through May 31, 2012) accounting for 52% of the total earnings at the North American box office during May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-May_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-May-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_North_America">Outside North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Outside North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The film became the fourth-highest grossing film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alltime-overseas_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-alltime-overseas-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing Disney-distributed film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas2_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas2-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing 2012 film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-2012_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-2012-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> and the highest-grossing superhero film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter16_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter16-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> It opened Wednesday, April 25, 2012, in 10 countries, earning $17.1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline3_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline3-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> It opened in 29 more countries on April 26 and 27, earning $73.1 million in three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline4_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline4-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> Through Sunday, April 29, it earned an opening-weekend total of $185.1 million from 39 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> It was in first place at the box office outside North America for four consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter15_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter15-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter17_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter17-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter18_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter18-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> The film set opening-day records in New Zealand, Malaysia and Iceland, a single-day record in the Philippines, as well as both single- and opening-day records in Singapore and in Thailand. It also earned the second highest-grossing opening day in Australia ($6.2 million), behind <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>, in Mexico, in the Philippines and in Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline5_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline5-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline3_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline3-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline4_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline4-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter10_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter10-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter11_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter11-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> It set opening-weekend records in many territories, including Mexico, Brazil, Ecuador, Bolivia, Taiwan, the Philippines, Hong Kong, the United Arab Emirates, Argentina (the latter was first surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Madagascar_3:_Europe%27s_Most_Wanted" title="Madagascar 3: Europe's Most Wanted">Madagascar 3: Europe's Most Wanted</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-argentina_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-argentina-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> Peru and Central America (the last two overtaken by <i><a href="/wiki/Ice_Age:_Continental_Drift" title="Ice Age: Continental Drift">Ice Age: Continental Drift</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iceage4_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-iceage4-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter12_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter12-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deadline7_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-deadline7-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> It also earned the second largest five-day opening in Australia ($20.2 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_201-2"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aus-opening_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aus-opening-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the UK, Ireland and Malta, the film earned £2.5 million ($4.1 million) on its opening day<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME2_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-NME2-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> and £15.8 million ($25.7 million) during the weekend,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK-opening_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK-opening-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> setting an opening-weekend record for a superhero film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter11_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter11-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitaspy2_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitaspy2-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the market's highest-grossing superhero film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK-top_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK-top-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> a record surpassed by <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> during the same summer season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKR-UK_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKR-UK-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> In Latin America, it became the highest-grossing film ($207 million)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter20_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter20-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> and the first film to earn more than $200 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter19_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter19-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> It also became the highest-grossing film in the Philippines, in Singapore and in Indonesia (both the Philippines and Indonesia were surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> in 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxcom-Avengers_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxcom-Avengers-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indonesia-im3_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-indonesia-im3-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Records</dt>
</dl>
<p>Upon release, the film set several records at the <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> box office, including the following:</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width:99%;">
<tr>
<th>Box office record</th>
<th>Record details</th>
<th>Previous record</th>
<th>Ref.</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Opening weekend for any film</td>
<td>$207,438,708</td>

<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ninefig"><sup>*</sup></span> While eight films have reached $100 million after two days, the film's gross by the end of the second day exceeded all of them, including <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>, which previously held the record.<br/></p>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="433" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg/170px-Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg/255px-Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg/340px-Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a> at the film's Toronto premiere. Ruffalo's performance was critically lauded.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reported a 92% approval rating with an average rating of 8/10 based on 301 reviews. The website's consensus reads, "With a script that never forgets its heroes' humanity and no shortage of superpowered set pieces, The Avengers lives up to its hype -- and raises the bar for Marvel at the movies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, the film achieved an average score of 69 out of 100 based on 43 reviews, signifying "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> reported that audiences gave the film a rare A+ grade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crit1_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crit1-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> of <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> gave a positive review of the film, remarking, "It's clamorous, the save-the-world story is one everyone's seen time and again, and the characters have been around for more than half a century in 500 comic book issues. But Whedon and his cohorts have managed to stir all the personalities and ingredients together so that the resulting dish, however familiar, is irresistibly tasty again."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter9_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter9-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> To <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a>, the film epitomized an exceptional blockbuster. "It's also the blockbuster," Travers said, "I saw in my head when I imagined a movie that brought together the idols of the Marvel world in one shiny, stupendously exciting package. It's <i>Transformers</i> with a brain, a heart and a working sense of humor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollz_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollz-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> Justin Chang of <i>Variety</i> wrote, "Like a superior, state-of-the-art model built from reconstituted parts, Joss Whedon's buoyant, witty and robustly entertaining superhero smash-up is escapism of a sophisticated order, boasting a tonal assurance and rich reserves of humor that offset the potentially lumbering and unavoidably formulaic aspects of this 143-minute team-origin story."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety6_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Variety6-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i>Los Angeles Times</i> complimented the film's frenetic pace,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes2_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes2-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> commented that it "provides its fans with exactly what they desire. Whether it is exactly what they deserve is arguable".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebert_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> Conversely, <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> believed that "while <i>The Avengers</i> is hardly worth raging about, its failures are significant and dispiriting. The light, amusing bits cannot overcome the grinding, hectic emptiness, the bloated cynicism that is less a shortcoming of this particular film than a feature of the genre."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The performances of several cast members was a frequent topic in the critiques. In particular, Mark Ruffalo's portrayal of Dr. Bruce Banner/the Hulk was well-received by commentators. Joe Neumaier opined that his performance was superior to the rest of the cast; "Ruffalo is the revelation, turning Banner into a wry reservoir of calm ready to become a volcano."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydaily_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> '​s <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Lane" title="Anthony Lane">Anthony Lane</a> proclaimed Ruffalo's acting to be one of the film's highlights—alongside Downey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> '​s <a href="/wiki/Karina_Longworth" title="Karina Longworth">Karina Longworth</a> concluded: "Ruffalo successfully refreshes the Hulk myth, playing Banner as an adorably bashful nerd-genius who, in contrast to the preening hunks on the team, knows better than to draw attention to himself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-villagevoice_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-villagevoice-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> Travers asserted that the actor resonated a "scruffy warmth and humor" vibe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollz_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollz-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> while Turan felt that he surpassed predecessors <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bana" title="Eric Bana">Eric Bana</a> in playing the character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes2_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes2-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Owen Gleiberman of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> wrote that "the smartest thing the filmmakers did was to get Mark Ruffalo to play Bruce Banner as a man so sensitive that he's at war, every moment, with himself. (The film finally solves the Hulk problem: He's a lot more fun in small doses.)"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW-review_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-review-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Referring to Downey, Joe Morgenstein of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>—despite complimenting Downey's performance—favored his work in <i>Iron Man</i> over his acting in <i>The Avengers</i>: "His Iron Man is certainly a team player, but Mr. Downey comes to the party with two insuperable superpowers: a character of established sophistication—the industrialist/inventor Tony Stark, a sharp-tongued man of the world—and his own quicksilver presence that finds its finest expression in self-irony."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj22_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj22-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> Neumaier praised Evans, stating that he accurately conveyed his character's internal conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydaily_236-1"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Commentators appreciated the character development and dialogue. <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> reviewer <a href="/wiki/Christy_Lemire" title="Christy Lemire">Christy Lemire</a> wrote that the script "sparkles as brightly as the special effects; these people may be wearing ridiculous costumes but they're well fleshed-out underneath."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-associatedpress_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-associatedpress-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> Scott suggested that certain parts of the film permeated a charm that he felt was similar to the western film <i><a href="/wiki/Rio_Bravo_(film)" title="Rio Bravo (film)">Rio Bravo</a></i> (1959).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_235-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> Longworth felt that while Whedon's script demonstrated the backstory of the characters, the film does not explore it "in a substantive way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-villagevoice_238-1"><a href="#cite_note-villagevoice-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Marvel%27s_The_Avengers" title="List of accolades received by Marvel's The Avengers">List of accolades received by Marvel's The Avengers</a></div>
<p><i>The Avengers</i> has garnered numerous awards and nominations, including an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Award" title="British Academy Film Award">British Academy Film Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Visual Effects</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcademyAwards_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-AcademyAwards-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAFTAAwards_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAFTAAwards-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> The film has also been nominated for three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Awards" title="Critics' Choice Movie Awards">Critics' Choice Movie Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012CriticChoice_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012CriticChoice-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> thirteen <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a> (winning three),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PeoplesChoice_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-PeoplesChoice-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> eleven <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a> (winning two),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice2_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice2-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice3_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice3-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> six <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a> (winning four),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SaturnAwards_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-SaturnAwards-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> and six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VES_Awards" title="VES Awards">VES Awards</a> (winning two), as well as the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for Best Dramatic Presentation Long Form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VESAwards_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-VESAwards-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels">Sequels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sequels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron"><i>Avengers: Age of Ultron</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Avengers: Age of Ultron">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></div>
<p>A sequel, titled <i>Avengers: Age of Ultron</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AvengersAgeofUltron_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAgeofUltron-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> written and directed by Whedon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety-August2012_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-August2012-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> is scheduled to be released on May 1, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-August2012_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-August2012-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> Much of the cast returns, with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Olsen" title="Elizabeth Olsen">Elizabeth Olsen</a> as <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_Witch" title="Scarlet Witch">Scarlet Witch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Taylor-Johnson" title="Aaron Taylor-Johnson">Aaron Taylor-Johnson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Quicksilver_(comics)" title="Quicksilver (comics)">Quicksilver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bettany" title="Paul Bettany">Paul Bettany</a> as <a href="/wiki/Vision_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Vision (Marvel Comics)">Vision</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Spader" title="James Spader">James Spader</a> as <a href="/wiki/Ultron" title="Ultron">Ultron</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoUCast_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-AoUCast-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avengers:_Infinity_War"><i>Avengers: Infinity War</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Avengers: Infinity War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2014, <i>Avengers: Infinity War</i> was announced, with <i>Part 1</i> scheduled to be released on May 4, 2018 and <i>Part 2</i> on May 3, 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InfinityWar_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-InfinityWar-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Avengers_(2012_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ol>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span> As part of the deal transferring the distribution rights of <i>Marvel's The Avengers</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(production_company)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (production company)">The Walt Disney Studios</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety4_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Variety4-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Paramount's logo appears in the films' promotional materials and merchandise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ParamountVariety_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-ParamountVariety-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a> is credited at the end of the film.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^</a></b></span> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Movieline" title="Movieline">Movieline</a></i>, producer Kevin Feige stated that the Tesseract is based on the <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_Cube" title="Cosmic Cube">Cosmic Cube</a> from Marvel comics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieline_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-movieline-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> After <i><a href="/wiki/Thor:_The_Dark_World" title="Thor: The Dark World">Thor: The Dark World</a></i>, in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/CraveOnline" title="CraveOnline">CraveOnline</a></i>, he stated that it was also the Space <a href="/wiki/Infinity_Gems" title="Infinity Gems">Infinity Stone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CraveOnline3_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-CraveOnline3-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3"><b><a href="#ref_3">^</a></b></span> Feige confirmed in an <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> that the "master" in the post-credits scene is <a href="/wiki/Thanos" title="Thanos">Thanos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmpirePodcast_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmpirePodcast-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-soundworks-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-soundworks_18-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Supervising Sound Editor, Sound Designer, and Re-recording Mixer Christopher Boyes at 3:22 of video interview, <span class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://soundworkscollection.com/theavengers" rel="nofollow">"The Sound of the Avengers"</a>. SoundWorks Collection (Colemanfilm Media Group). 2012. <a class="external text" href="http://www.webcitation.org/68C9nfvSB" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on June 5, 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 5,</span> 2012</span>. <q>Finally I thought, 'I just have to work with human voices.' ... I just started playing combinations and I would give them 10 to 15 variations of roars. And Joss listened to them and came back and said, 'I like this one,' and I went back and I looked at the ingredients of what was in that one. Turned out to be Mark Ruffalo, some Lou Ferrigno and a little bit of me and two people from <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. So I led with that and I started using those combinations but changing it up. But the great thing was that Mark Ruffalo had done an incredible [unintelligible] of variety so I was always blending him in. ... Lou Ferrigno seemed to have a real knack for just who this character was. ... They were always a component of it.</q></span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Avengers+%282012+film%29&amp;rft.btitle=The+Sound+of+the+Avengers&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsoundworkscollection.com%2Ftheavengers&amp;rft.pub=SoundWorks+Collection+%28Colemanfilm+Media+Group%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

The film is planned to premier in 3D in May of next year. Stellan Skarsgård confirms to <i>TT Spektra</i> that he will play the same role as in the upcoming <i>Thor</i>: Doctor Selvig. Oh, that must mean something, who's that?' and they start to learn and they start to dig deeper.</q></span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Avengers+%282012+film%29&amp;rft.atitle=Kevin+Feige+Avengers+Spoiler+Podcast&amp;rft.aufirst=All&amp;rft.aulast=Plumb&amp;rft.au=Plumb%2C+All&amp;rft.date=April+30%2C+2012&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.empireonline.com%2Fnews%2Fstory.asp%3FNID%3D33806&amp;rft.jtitle=Empire&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="padding-left:0;padding-right:0;">
